Bodies from Food Poisoning at Oujia Road Restaurant Sent for Autopsy 152

Leftover Food Sent to Government Office

Waiting for Thorough Investigation and Comforting Families

At the Xie Shunxing Restaurant at 59 Oujia Road in Hongkou, ten diners suffered food poisoning after eating the previous day (the 28th), and died one after another, resulting in an unprecedented tragedy. After the local constable reported the incident, the district court sent personnel to verify that the ten bodies of Gu Koulang (i.e., Wang Koulang), Luo Honglin, Lu Jiayu, Ding Fushan, Ma Kuisheng, Zhao Xiaolaohan, Xu Zhenhong, Zhou Xiaoerzi, Jiang Xiaogenzi, and a certain person named Jia were indeed caused by poisoning. As reported in yesterday's newspaper, it is now known that after the public prosecutor Wu Deying and the coroner Xuan Zhiming examined the bodies, they determined that they were poisoned. However, it was not easy to identify what kind of poison it was. In order to clarify the truth, they designated the body of Gu Koulang (from Chongming, living at 147 Fengtian Road) from these ten bodies to be transported to the Zhenru Forensic Institute for autopsy and examination. Cao Aixiang (age 26), a rickshaw puller from Taixing, residing at 26 Shuxingli, Yangjiabang, Zhabei, also ate at the restaurant that day. He originally intended to return home, but suddenly felt abdominal pain, dizziness, and weak legs, so he temporarily went to his friend Xu Jinfa's house (on the second floor of 10 Yangjiabang Road) to rest on the bed for a while. Unexpectedly, in a short time, his abdominal pain was like twisting, and he rolled around on the bed in chaos, and then died of breath. Later, the police learned of this and reported it to the Linping Road Police Station. Yesterday morning, he ordered Li A'er, the local constable of the 23rd Bao and 2nd Tu, to file a petition with the district court for inspection. In the afternoon, he sent Prosecutor Xie and Coroner Xuan to investigate, and it was determined that he also died of poisoning, and he ordered the family to coffin him. It was found that Jiang Xiaogenzi, who lived in Hongzhen, had a big meal at the restaurant and suddenly felt nauseous when he got home. Soon after, he vomited, and the mess was all over the floor. His family fed the vomit to the chicken, but unexpectedly, the huge rooster fell to the ground and died immediately after eating it. Those who saw it were horrified, which proved that its toxic properties were quite violent and that it was extremely rapid. After the incident, the police station sent police to take all the remaining vegetables in the restaurant, such as fish, meat, fresh chicken, and vegetables, as well as a whole basket of rice and two small wine urns (commonly known as pig gall urns), each containing half a basket of sorghum wine, to the police station. Yesterday afternoon, he ordered Ling Renjie, the local constable of the 23rd Bao and 5th Tu, to send all the above items to the district court by car. He was ordered to transfer them to the Zhenru Forensic Institute for chemical examination. On one side, the constable and the family members of the deceased, such as Ding Lanqin, father of the deceased Ding Fushan, Zhao Kunbao, father of the deceased Zhao Xiaolaohan, Lu Wangshi, wife of the deceased Lu Jiayu, Jiang Fenglou, father of the deceased Jiang Xiaogenzi, etc., reported to the district court, requesting redress. After being interrogated, they were ordered to leave and wait for the police station to bring the restaurant staff to court for a thorough investigation.

Shanghai Telephone Bureau Adds Minhang Telephone 153

At the request of the Shanghai County Government, the Shanghai Telephone Bureau of the Ministry of Communications is building a Minhang telephone. In order to rectify the city's appearance and improve traffic control, the Municipal Public Security Bureau, together with the Municipal Public Utilities Bureau and the Municipal Public Works Bureau, sent personnel to the city's key intersections to assess the situation and determine the order of importance for the installation of traffic lights to meet the needs. It has been learned from the Guomin News Agency reporters that red and green lights will be installed at eleven key and secondary key locations, and seventeen vehicle stop lines will be marked. The road names are recorded as follows: Zhabei (1) Baoshan Road and Henan Road intersection, (2) Qimei Road and Xiangyin Road intersection, (3) Datong Road and Xinmin Road intersection, Nanshi (4) Xie Bridge, (5) Dongmen Road, (6) Xiaodongmen, (7) Shangwen Road, (8) Damatou. The above are key locations. Zhabei (9) Datong Road and Gonghe Road intersection, (10) Baoshan Road and Qiujiang Road intersection, (11) Wuzhen Road Bridge Head. The above are secondary key locations. It is planned to install red and green traffic lights at the following eleven locations first: (1) Baoshan Road intersection, (2) Datong Road intersection, (3) Xinmin Road intersection, (4) Datong Road and Gonghe Road intersection, (5) Baoshan Road and Qiujiang Road intersection, (6) Wuzhen Road Bridge Head, (7) Tongji Road and Baoshan Road intersection, (8) Hengfeng Road Bridge Head, (9) Wujiaochang, (10) Xinqiao Bridge Head, (11) Gonghe Road, (12) Xie Bridge, (13) Dongmen Road, (14) Xiaodongmen, (15) Shangwenmen (16) Damatou Street Bund, (17) Laoximen. Vehicle stop lines and no-parking lines will be marked at the above seventeen locations respectively. The Public Utilities Bureau, Public Security Bureau, and Public Works Bureau have jointly made detailed plans for the installation of control platforms, red and green switches, and vehicle stop lines. The cost is estimated at 8,565 yuan. It is reported that it has been submitted to the municipal government for approval and will begin construction soon.

Wang Xitang, Who Killed Out of Jealousy, Sentenced to Life Imprisonment 157

Lin Axiang, a woman from Shaoxing, was twenty-six years old this year. She married Wang Wenshao in the countryside in her early years. After Wang died of illness, Axiang came to Shanghai to make a living. In November of the fifteenth year of the Republic of China, she met and cohabited with Wang Xitang, a fellow villager who worked as a boatman. Later, Axiang invested 600 yuan and handed it over to Wang to purchase a barge to operate the business independently. Over time, Wang liked the new and tired of the old and fell in love with someone else, neglecting Axiang's daily life. In September of the twenty-first year, Wang's old father came forward to negotiate and agreed that Axiang would pay 400 yuan to Wang Xitang, and the two separated. In February of the twenty-second year, Axiang remarried to Peng Quanshi (age 24), a Tongzhou native who worked as a copper polisher, and cohabited at 6 Xinleli, Mintini Yin Road, Nanyang Bridge, French Concession. Unexpectedly, Wang Xitang was still unwilling. On the morning of the 28th of that month, he waited at Xinleli. When Peng went out, soaked in water and returned home, he caught up with Peng and fired several shots, killing Peng and fleeing without a trace. At that time, when Wang was fleeing, Axiang and Peng's brothers caught a glimpse of him and reported it to the French patrol house to arrest him. Wang hid in the Hongkou area of Pudong, because he was engaged in a water-based boat life and his whereabouts were uncertain, and the detectives could not arrest him. Until about 5:00 PM on October 14th of this year, Lin Axiang passed by Oujia Road and happened to bump into Wang. She called the 490 patrolman and arrested Wang at the Jiaxing Road Patrol House. After learning that the incident occurred in the French Concession, he was immediately sent to the French Patrol House. After investigation by Detective Zhou Buguang, he was transferred to the Second Special District Court. The legal representative of the police department filed a public prosecution for murder. The details of the trial have been recorded in previous newspapers. The case has been repeatedly heard by Judge Xiong Huiping, and witnesses have been summoned for investigation, and lawyers have been appointed for defense. It has been announced that the case has been concluded. Yesterday was the date of sentencing. At 10:30 AM, Judge Xiong came to the first criminal court and ordered the defendant to be brought to court. After a brief interrogation, Wang Xitang was sentenced to life imprisonment for premeditated murder. During the appeal period, he will be held at the detention center for further instructions.

Double Fire Alarm in a Day 158

Baole An Road: At the end of Baole An Road, Shikaotuo Road, in a straw shed, Ni Liucai, a native of Yancheng, lived by growing vegetables and raising pigs. Yesterday afternoon at about 5:30, a fire was accidentally left on the straw shed while cooking dinner, and it suddenly started to burn. At that time, the north wind was very strong, and in an instant, twelve straw sheds were burned down. Fortunately, no one was injured. Later, the fire brigade rushed to the scene to rescue, and it took an hour to put out the fire. The arsonist was arrested by the post police and taken to the Public Security Bureau for punishment.

Jumen Road: Yesterday morning at about 8:00, a fire broke out at Wanshunxing, a cigarette and paper shop opened by Chen Tai at No. 125 Jumen Road in the southern city. In an instant, the fire burst through the roof. The nearby post police notified fire brigades in various districts, and fire trucks quickly rushed to the scene to do their utmost to extinguish the fire. It took about an hour for the fire to be extinguished. It is estimated that three buildings were burned down, and the fire spread to the neighboring houses of Xi Jiadong and Liang Guofu at No. 126, with a total loss estimated at several thousand yuan. The scene was chaotic at the time. Chen Shengzhou, the patrol officer of the Liyuan Police Substation in charge of the area, went to suppress the chaos and investigate the cause of the fire. Chen Tai, an arsonist from Shaoxing, was taken to the bureau for interrogation.

Foreign Detective Fined 159

Lu Shilin, a detective from the Narcotics Division of the General Police Station, was recently sued by Xu Qingxiang, who hired lawyers Yan Liang Bohua to file a complaint with the First Special Court for injury and other charges. The main points of the indictment stated that Xu was chatting with a friend at No. 12 Ankang Lane, Erma Road at 1:00 AM on October 30th, when he was inexplicably struck by Lu Detective with a pistol butt, causing swelling and bruising to his left eye, pain in his chest, and severe pain in his left shoulder blade. A forensic examination was conducted by the court, so he specially filed a private prosecution, requesting that Lu Detective be summoned to the court to be punished according to the law. Yesterday afternoon, Judge Wu Tingqi presided over the eighth criminal court to summon the defendant. The defendant denied committing the assault. After the lawyer Liang Bohua, representing the plaintiff, and lawyer Fan Gang, representing the defendant, debated, Judge Wu ruled that Lu Shilin should be fined 50 yuan, and 50 yuan in cash should be paid as bail during the appeal period.

Mad Dog Bites Dog Catcher 160

Though mad dog dies,

Hunter also injured.

The Municipal Health Bureau has been dispatching personnel to various streets in Pudong to catch stray dogs for several days. All of them were caught without exception. At 2:00 PM yesterday, the dog catchers drove to the Qichangzhan area to work. Suddenly, they encountered a mad dog. The catchers surrounded it, but the mad dog became even more frantic, rushing and biting wildly. Four or five passersby were bitten on the spot, and the dog catching foreman was also bitten several times and seriously injured. He returned to Pudong by rickshaw that night for treatment. The mad dog died in a hail of knives in an instant, and its body was buried to prevent the spread of the disease.

Plea to Preserve Public Docks 165

Xing Zhigang, the representative of the Pudong Westbound Shipping Industry, previously submitted a request to the Shanghai Municipal Government to organize water transportation in the South Shanghai area and preserve the location of various public docks to maintain the safety of the shipping industry. Yesterday, the municipal government replied, stating, "Regarding the section on wooden rafts obstructing traffic, the Public Security Bureau, Public Utilities Bureau, and Land Bureau jointly reported that because of the lease of the coastline, it is not appropriate to immediately ban it before a fundamental solution is found. Moreover, the locations of various public docks in the South Shanghai area were reserved during the previous coastline planning for the berthing of various public vessels. All vessels owned by the shipping households can freely berth there. If the location is too narrow and insufficient, they can request the Land Bureau to designate a dedicated coastline and pay fees to obtain a license for use." Accordingly, in addition to instructions, this is further approved for notification.

Spring and Autumn

Little Western Paradise 176

— Written by Zhang Henshui

Chapter 5: Fawning Smiles Meet Wan Visage Lit by a Lamp; Empty Stomachs Drive One to Imitate Refined Airs with Powder

For a good long while, he finally smiled faintly: "I've seen the person more than once, and I've talked to her. Whether it works out or not is irrelevant. What I want to know is, what exactly do they plan to do with this girl?" Xiao Ji shrugged his shoulders slightly twice and said, "If Old Master Jia is willing to take a concubine, it's easy to arrange. They aren't relying on the girl to make a fortune. It's just that they can't make ends meet, and marrying the girl off would give her a place to settle down and make a living. That way, even two generations of his family won't starve to death. When it comes to money, I don't think they can possibly ask for an exorbitant amount." Jia Duocai exhaled two puffs of smoke before replying in a rather nonchalant manner, "I'm just afraid they don't quite understand these things. You think people spend money to take concubines, wouldn't they go to big cities like Shanghai and Beijing to find them? Why come to this hard place of Xi'an to find one? I'm just acting out of kindness, seeing that this little girl and her family of three are very pitiful, and I'm willing to give them a helping hand. If their intention is just to escape with their lives, that's easy to handle. But if they want to get rich, I wouldn't dare to take it on. Please ask them to find someone else." As he spoke, he crossed one leg over the other and swayed it constantly. Xiao Ji thought to himself, "The rich are truly devils. Others barely give an inch, and they immediately tighten their grip." So he said, "Of course, they just want to escape with their lives. Don't worry, those ignorant women wouldn't be able to play any tricks that could outsmart you, Old Master Jia, would they?" Hearing this, Jia Duocai took out his cigarette holder and tapped the ash into the spittoon, with a slight smile. Xiao Ji said, "Old Master Jia, why don't you set a time?" At this point, Jia Duocai was really too embarrassed to keep declining, so he raised his hand to scratch his head and then smiled faintly, "I think you guys should set it. If I set the time, it would seem like I'm the one inviting them. Women's words are hard to say; they're bound to act coy. I think it's better to leave it to chance." (78)

A Returned Traveler's Tale from Chao Mountain 177

— By Fang'an

When counting the places where one can enjoy plum blossoms, Chao Mountain has long stood out as a unique peak. The mountain is located in Hangzhou County, Zhejiang Province, between Linping and Tangqi. There is a highway accessible by motorcycles and buses. During the flowering season, entering its realm is truly like entering "a dwelling atop Mount Qunyu, entering the land of myriad fragrances," as the late Kang Nanhai inscribed in a couplet. Since the remains of the master artist Wu Changshuo were laid to rest here, famous figures have flocked to visit, one after another. It is said that Chairman Chiang himself once visited with his wife. This October, the plum blossoms on the ridge bloomed early. The old plum trees in the mountains have already begun to flower, dotting the branches like lingering snow after a clear sky, creating a spectacular sight. Next to the Song Plum Pavilion, the Bao Ci Temple's Fragrance Ocean Tower, which was destroyed by bandits in the past, is being rebuilt with donations from Mr. Xi Guansheng of Panyu. Construction is already underway, and by the time it is completed, it will probably be at the height of the plum blossoms and snow competing for spring. The local gentry, together with the temple monk Guang Zhou, are also planning to revive the temple, sparing no effort. Recently, they transplanted an old plum tree from the ruins of the former residence of the Southern Song Dynasty's Lord of Fortune. Its branches are gnarled and sprawling, surpassing the previous trees, and its mossy traces are a true Zhao family treasure. Guanshengyuan has also newly opened a plum forest, all striving for the sake of this famous mountain's enterprise. The end of winter is easy to encounter, and a stay during the flowering season is sure to be a refreshing experience. The Haiyun Cave has also been fully renovated, with its serene environment and beautiful scenery comparable to the misty clouds and purple mists of the lake, and new roads have been built, eliminating the need to trek over the mountain ridges. However, the Miaoxi Temple in the mountains was destroyed by fire last month, turning the magnificent temple halls into ashes, a truly great disaster for this famous mountain. Mr. Shi Liangcai also visited last month. Mr. Shi had previously built three rooms within the Bao Ci Temple, and when the temple was destroyed, these three rooms stood alone, unscathed. Now that Mr. Shi has unfortunately been attacked by bandits, the spirit of the mountain must be mourning endlessly.

Following the tea room attendant's instructions, I went over and opened the door. I indeed discovered that one of my relatives was lying in bed, intertwined with a woman. Seeing me, he hurriedly put on his clothes and got up, his face flushed red, as if filled with endless shame. I thought to myself silently, "Shanghai is truly a den of iniquity. The city is truly a place of crime!"

I urge young people not to be infatuated with the pleasures of the senses. Quickly rouse your spirits! You must know that great achievements are built on a firm will.

Snippets 178

— (Jiaoxin)

How small is a single drop, how insignificant is a single second? Yet one's entire life, from infancy to adulthood to old age, and finally to passing away, unfolds within these seconds.

Little brother doesn't need their kisses, yet they keep showering him with kisses. It's always the way with things in the world: what's not needed is not considered rare, but what's needed is impossible to obtain.

The Sins of the City 179

— Baling

People generally say, "Shanghai is a den of iniquity." At first, I didn't quite believe this statement. But now, I deeply feel that this statement is indeed true. Because in the recent past, there was an ironclad fact that gave me a powerful proof. The fact is like this:

A relative came from the countryside. Deeming me worthy, he came to visit me. Of course, as the host, I had an inescapable duty to entertain him. So, everything from eating meals to watching movies to going to the amusement park, I took care of him one by one. Finally, I borrowed room X at the XX Inn as a place for him to stay.

For financial reasons, we borrowed a single room, with two people sleeping in one bed. I thought that in early winter, this would be very suitable. So, we settled down to sleep. Because I had traveled a lot during the day, I was very tired. Before long, I was dreaming of the Duke of Zhou, sleeping soundly and snoring.

Unexpectedly, as dawn approached, I woke up and found that my relative was nowhere to be found. This was truly very strange. Finally, I learned from the tea room attendant's report that he had opened another room, and there was a woman accompanying him.

Drifting Fragrances: A Record 180

— Originally written by Princess Der Ling of the Qing Dynasty, translated by Qin Shouou

However, after Emperor Guangxu passed away, because there was no grand mourning ceremony held, no relics were sent to Fengtian to be stored. This was a special measure that violated the customs of previous dynasties and cannot be considered a reasonable approach. The reasonable approach would have been to respectfully transport the Emperor's daily attire or familiar objects to Fengtian to be treasured. This practice was initiated by the first emperor of the Qing Dynasty, Emperor Shunzhi, to show that he did not forget his homeland and to elevate the status of the ancient palaces in Shengjing. Since the imperial family had all moved to the interior, the palaces in Fengtian inevitably became neglected and unoccupied. Now that these relics of past emperors were stored inside, and a high-ranking military officer was specially stationed with a team of Manchurian soldiers year-round, these unoccupied palaces would not be completely uninhabited, and their status would be elevated in an imperceptible way.

We started with the first palace and visited each one in turn. This first palace contained the relics of the first two emperors of the Qing Dynasty, Emperor Shunzhi and Emperor Kangxi. As soon as we entered, the Empress Dowager began to explain to us like a teacher in a classroom. Her eloquence was already excellent, but now she intentionally portrayed the history of these two emperors as grand as could possibly be. If we closed our eyes and only listened to her endless and eloquent speech, we would surely regard these two emperors as gods. Moreover, we would deeply believe that she was indeed very familiar with and cared about their past deeds. (188)

Walking the Underworld 181

— Wubian

"Walking the underworld" is not just a strange tale, it's simply a joke. However, in the countryside, people still frighten each other with it, and everyone firmly believes that it's true. As a result, those who "walk the underworld" sell their "ghostly schemes," and no one ever breaks this darkness.

Isn't this just a huge joke? How can living people who eat and wear clothes in this world go to serve in the underworld and do the work of catching people? But the villagers still firmly believe it. Their reason for believing is: they say that there are bailiffs in the Yang world, so of course there are bailiffs in the Yin world; there are constables in the Yang world, so of course there are constables in the Yin world. If the Yin world wants to capture living people in the Yang world, it naturally needs living people to lead the way. So, they also call this "walking the underworld" "ghost bailiff."

Now let me give you an introduction to this "walking the underworld": the one who "walks the underworld" is also an ordinary person, but most of them are either bored or scoundrels. It is said that after the King of Hell in the underworld appoints him to be the "underworld walker" of a certain area, when someone in that area is about to die, he leads the Ox-Headed and Horse-Faced demons to the home of that person to capture them. As for the moment when he leads them, he seems to have received a premonition, suddenly falling to the ground as if he has stopped breathing and died for a while, and then slowly regaining consciousness. Once conscious, he tells people about his experience of leading the capture and the name of the person who died. Those who see his condition and hear his story at that time all believe him one hundred and twenty percent and voluntarily spread the word.

However, there are flaws in the "underworld walker's" performance after all, but the deceived are not easily aware of them. Speaking of this flaw, it is his deceptive scheme. It turns out, according to his own account, he has a register, and this register lists the time of death of the person who is about to die. When this time arrives, he leads the Ox-Headed and Horse-Faced demons to capture them. But he also tells people that one can bribe in the underworld. If you give a considerable bribe, your name can be removed from the register, and you can live a few more lifespans. Since no one is not afraid of death, his scheme is sold.

This is really not a strange tale, it's simply a joke. However, he—the "underworld walker"—is able to sell his ghostly scheme every time under the frightening and believing of the masses. From this, it can be seen that the customs of the countryside and the knowledge of the villagers are really pitifully closed and deplorably shallow!

Beware of Explosions 182

Places Visited

Mandarin Duck Lake 183

— Shuzi

Autumn is deep, and the autumn scenery will gradually disappear as the seasons change. The mournful cries of the lonely geese flying through the sky and returning south deeply stir my aimless emotions and arouse my desire to travel.

Mandarin Duck Lake, just mentioning this name makes people feel intoxicated. In the past, I had also yearned for the beautiful and charming lake scenery there, the picturesque lotus ponds. I had also fantasized about throwing myself into the intoxicating embrace of the mandarin ducks. However, driven by life, fantasies are ultimately fantasies, even though I have frequently traveled the Shanghai-Hangzhou road in recent years.

This yearning hope has finally been realized. On a Double Tenth Festival morning, Mr. C and I took the 7:55 AM express train to Shanghai and Zhapu. After two hours of travel, we arrived in Jiaxing.

"Going to the lake? Going boating?" Outside the station gate, there was a chorus of such voices. As we walked out of the station gate, the village girls crowded on both sides, wearing simple clothes, with gentle smiles and the pure Jiaxing accent, were soliciting every passenger who came out of the station. These are the boat girls who make South Lake even more charming and colorful!

The so-called "Lu and Lu legacy" is naturally no exception in a place like Jiaxing. For example, the East Garden on the banks of Mandarin Duck Lake is the leading teahouse in this area. We first had some tea in the East Garden and discussed our plans for touring the lake, in order to appreciate the natural scenery. So, we walked out of the East Garden, bought a small boat, and rowed across the railway bridge on the Shanghai-Hangzhou road. The Rain-Mist Tower, standing alone in the center of South Lake, immediately caught our eyes. Three or five small boats floated on the lake surface, seemingly without direction, drifting among the lotus leaves. The cool breeze caressed our faces, and along with the sounds of rowing oars, came the faintly audible lotus-picking songs of the village girls. This picturesque scene is so worth appreciating and full of poetic charm! Looking up at the sky again, we felt as if we were dissolving into nature and forgetting the mundane world.

As I sat in the boat, looking around at the furnishings in the cabin, I inadvertently discovered a poem given to the boat girl by a tourist. I don't know who wrote this poem, but the lingering flavor between the lines fully expresses that it was written by a sentimental person. So, I transcribed it with my pen:

"Meeting so巧, loving like glue, our hearts are sealed, Heaven knows! You are not pretty, I am not handsome, yet we are so good to each other! Spring flowers bloom, spring waters stir, we are all moved by spring's sentiment! Time is old, separation is too late, please recall those days, this day! Farewell, farewell, don't be sad, please recall those days, this day!

Spring 1934, in the midst of a frustrated life, I went mad to Jiaxing, traveled alone to South Lake, and after getting drunk, I was inspired and wrote the above lines to comfort Miss Jun as a memento of Baishuilu."

After wandering on the lake for half a day, we returned to Shanghai at dusk, but the day's excitement still lingered in my mind like smoke.

Education News

National Vocational and Labor Exhibition Sponsored by the Ministry of Education 184

Opens Today at the Examination Yuan in Nanjing for Ten Days

No Ceremony Held; Exhibits from Thirty Provinces and Cities

The Ministry of Education-sponsored 23rd National Vocational School and Primary and Secondary School Labor Science Achievement Exhibition opened today (the 1st) at the Examination Yuan in Nanjing. Due to space limitations, the conference did not hold an opening ceremony. Only officials from various agencies, foreign guests, and teachers and staff from schools in Nanjing were invited to visit. The details of the conference are recorded below:

Record of Preparations for the Achievement Exhibition Zhou Bangdao 185

The Ministry of Education, in order to promote the implementation of vocational education and labor education, has held a National Vocational School and Primary and Secondary School Labor Science Achievement Exhibition. As it opens, I would like to briefly record the preparation process.

On April 4th of this year, the Ministry of Education formulated the Exhibition Regulations, consisting of five chapters and twenty-two articles, and issued them to the education departments and bureaus of various provinces and cities for compliance. The main points of the regulations are: 1. All public and registered private senior and junior vocational schools and primary and secondary schools in the country must participate. 2. The address of the Preparatory Committee shall be in Nanjing. 3. The exhibition period is set from October 10th to 20th, 1934. Provinces, cities, and districts should hold preliminary exhibitions separately before September 1st. 4. The scope of exhibits is divided into two parts: A. Main exhibits, which are (1) student practice achievements and work drawings from vocational schools, (2) student labor achievements and work drawings from primary and secondary schools. B. Supplementary exhibits, which are (1) achievements of educational administrative agencies, (2) achievements of school administration, (3) teaching achievements. 5. Submission procedures: after provinces, cities, and districts hold preliminary meetings, they should select representative achievements and send them to the Preparatory Committee before May 15th. 6. Those with excellent exhibits will be submitted by the Preparatory Committee to the Ministry of Education for commendation or certificates. Schools with particularly poor achievements or schools that must participate but do not submit achievements will be instructed to pay attention by the relevant departments. On June 21st and August 11th, telegraphic reminders were sent successively to urge the quick preparation and holding of preliminary exhibitions. Later, due to matters related to the exhibition venue, it was decided to change the opening to December 1st. On August 29th, a telegraphic order was issued to the education departments and bureaus of various provinces and cities, limiting them to sending the achievement products to the Preparatory Committee before the end of October, and selecting one or two staff members from each province and city to assist in the transportation, display, storage, and other matters related to the achievements. As of October 9th, several points were further notified: 1. Regarding the exemption from customs duties, the Ministry jointly with the Ministry of Finance printed tax-free passports. 2. Regarding the reduction of road transportation fees, the Ministry of Railways approved a reply stating that it could be handled in accordance with Article 1 of the Special Price Reduction Regulations for Railway Transportation of Educational Supplies. 3. Regarding the reduction of iron ship transportation fees, the Ministry of Communications approved a reply stating that it had instructed the state-run China Merchants Steam Navigation Company to charge half the original freight rate to show preferential treatment. These are the important matters that the Ministry of Education notified to the educational administrative agencies of various provinces and cities regarding the holding of the exhibition. The Preparatory Committee members, in accordance with Article 7 of the Exhibition Regulations, consisted of eleven to nineteen people. On July 28th, the Ministry of Education appointed Section Chief Dai Yingguan, Supervisor and Section Chief Zhong Daozan, Supervisors Tang Xifen, Gu Zhaolin, Zhou Bangdao, and five others as Preparatory Committee members, and Supervisors Tang, Gu, and Zhou temporarily served as Standing Committee members. On October 9th, Section Chiefs Zhong Lingxiu, Xu Yiqiao, Wu Yan Yin, Yu Dehui, and Specialist Li Jiaxiang were added as members (Xu later did not serve due to official business). Because the exhibition period was approaching and affairs were complicated, Division Chiefs Gu Shusen and Lei Zhen, Counselor Chen Panzao, Secretary Yi Keli, and Section Chief Guo Yunfeng were added as members on November 15th, and Division Chief Gu and Counselor Chen were designated as Standing Committee members.

The Preparatory Committee was originally divided into: 1. General Affairs and Reception Group, 2. Collection and Display Group, 3. Evaluation Group, 4. Editorial Group. Later, with the approval of the Vice Minister, the second group was changed to the Display and Layout Committee, and the third group was changed to the Evaluation Committee. Personnel were assigned successively. The director of the General Affairs Group was Gu Zhaolin, the general director was Zhou Yongnan, and the section chiefs were Lin Guanying, Peng Shuren, Zhong Zhong, Wei Xuezhi, and the staff were Shi Wei, Zhu Shusen, Wang Lun, Li Weiguang, Shen Lun, Yang Shiwei, etc. The chairman of the Display and Layout Committee was Tang Xifen, and the members were Gu Shusen, Wu Yan Yin, Chen Panzao, Li Jiaxiang, Zhong Lingxiu, etc. The staff were Liu Yiting, Yuan Dinghua, Yang Yanjun, Lou Yongqin, Weng Zhida, Shen Qingchi, Xue Tianhan, Jia Guoen, Yang Jingzhong, Shu Yu, Gao Zhicheng, Duan Dajia, Huang Longguang, Ding Yizhong, etc. The chairman of the Evaluation Committee was Gu Shusen, the director of the Editorial Group was Zhou Bangdao, the section chiefs were Yi Keli and Guo Lianfeng, and the staff were Wang Wanzhong, Huang Wenqi, You Chunmao, He Bolie, Yan Geli, Mo Guokang, Guan Zuxiong, Xie Zhuozi, Li Ruoxu, Lü Shutang, Zhang Guangxin, Zhao Chengyin, etc. Outside staff were hired: Zou Yitong, Lou Tongmao, Zhao Rusen, Ding Zhaonan, Chen Zhejin, Zhao Xue, Yan Shuji, Yin Changnian, Hu Yunlong, etc. The Preparatory Committee held thirteen meetings before and after, and convened one meeting with all staff members and representatives from various provinces and cities, and the various groups held several separate meetings. However, the progress of various affairs was often decided by informal ad hoc meetings.

The most difficult thing in this preparation was the issue of the exhibition venue. The Lizhi Society, the YMCA, the Overseas Chinese Reception Center, the Central University Auditorium, the Examination Yuan Mingzhi Building, the old site of the Ministry of Communications, and Chaotian Palace were successively consulted and surveyed, but they were not easy to resolve, either because of scheduling conflicts, insufficient space for display, or the high cost of renovations. In order to take into account the magnificent architecture, neat location, large area, and suitability for display and layout, it was decided to extend the exhibition period and use the Mingzhi Building as the venue. Dean Dai and Secretary-General Xu readily agreed to lend the entire building after the temporary examination of audit personnel and the closure of the Kaoquan meeting, which is very commendable. The Mingzhi Building is the examination venue of the Examination Yuan and has a close relationship with education. Moreover, the practical manufacturing and vocational subjects and labor subjects that have not been stipulated and are not easy to stipulate in the higher examinations, general examinations, and special examinations now have the opportunity to gather the national achievements in the "selecting the worthy and capable" venue of the country, the significance of which is also very thought-provoking.

The preparatory expenses were more than 11,200 yuan, which was approved by the Ministry of Education to be submitted to the Executive Yuan and then submitted to the National Government for approval, and was drawn from the preparatory funds for educational and cultural undertakings this year. Because the use was very strict and the budget was limited, all aspects were unusually frugal. The equipment required for the display, in addition to hundreds of self-made wooden ladder-shaped racks, row racks, and board racks, etc., the Ministry of Railways lent all eighty-one steel cabinets used in the National Railway Exhibition, which were transported from Tianjin to Nanjing. They were very elegant and saved costs. How grateful we are for this kind of convenience.

Those who participated this time, except for Xinjiang, Guizhou, Xikang, and Mongolia and Tibet, included Jiangsu, Zhejiang, Anhui, Jiangxi, Hebei, Henan, Shandong, Shanxi, Hubei, Hunan, Shaanxi, Gansu, Ningxia, Suiyuan, Chahar, Sichuan, Fujian, Guangdong, Guangxi, Yunnan, Nanjing, Shanghai, Beiping, Qingdao, Weihaiwei, and other twenty-six provinces and cities. The exhibits from the four northeastern provinces have been reported and are on their way. In total, there are more than 29,700 exhibits in twenty-eight categories. The exhibitors included 169 vocational schools, 337 middle schools, 139 normal schools, 868 primary schools, seven educational administrative agencies, nine social education agencies, and two educational academic groups. The venue was divided into four pavilions: Yanmao Hall was the first pavilion, the lower floor of Mingzhi Building was the second pavilion, the upper floor of Mingzhi Building was the third pavilion, and Xiji Hall was the fourth pavilion. The provincial and municipal units in each pavilion were allocated according to the number of exhibits. Large machinery was feared to damage the floor, so the cement ground and grass in front of the second pavilion were used as display locations, and two reed sheds were built in the empty space behind to store racks and exhibit boxes.

Regarding the display of exhibits, the main purpose was to [blank] the overall achievements of each province and city, so each province and city [blank] unit took the school category as the warp and the exhibit category as the weft. The order of the schools was vocational schools first, followed by middle schools, normal schools, and primary schools. Vocational schools were ordered by agriculture, industry, commerce, household affairs, and others. Middle schools, normal schools, and primary schools were ordered by crafts, agriculture, household affairs, teaching aids, and others. All exhibits that were damaged, inferior, worthless, or clearly counterfeit were removed in order to avoid losing the original intention of the exhibition.

The logo of this conference originally intended to draw a wheel, symbolizing the emerging industry, with the seal characters "heart" and "hand" superimposed on it, representing the joint training of hands and brains and the omnipotence of hands.

The entire Preparatory Committee

Photograph by Nanjing Zhonghua Photography Studio

Later, Vice Minister Duan came up with the idea of two male and female students jointly pushing the wheel forward, indicating effort, labor, cooperation, and progress. Mr. Xu Beihong, a professor at Central University, was specially invited to draw the manuscript, which has rich connotations and is worthy of cherishing.

In recent years, the Chinese people have paid considerable attention to vocational education and labor education, and those engaged in education have also made considerable efforts. However, there is no way to make an overall observation and comparison of the actual achievements. This time, gathering the national works in the capital for a solemn exhibition, the appropriateness of the need and the depth of the intention are self-evident. The colleagues secretly plan to select outstanding achievements after the evaluation is completed, take photos separately, and slightly imitate the idea of ​​the National Children's Model Works Collection published by the Central Exhibition of Elementary School Achievement Products in Japan, and publish the National Vocational Labor Excellent Achievement Collection (name not yet determined), so that it can be permanently observed and encouraged.

Due to limited ability and time, the colleagues of this association have prepared hastily, and there are many shortcomings. It is with a feeling of shame and fear that I hold the pen to describe this.

The Shanghai Municipal Council's Consideration of Educational Policy Will Continue According to the Original Plan 202

The Request of the Japanese Community Was Not Met

The Shanghai Municipal Council has recently reconsidered the case of the Japanese community's request to change the educational policy. At the Board of Directors meeting on the 28th of this month, it was decided to reply to the community, stating that the Council has considered the issue from various perspectives. At present, for the educational interests of any foreign community, it is impossible to further promote it, which would affect the Council's school construction plan. The Chinese education in the concession urgently needs to be improved and expanded, and the construction of (Chinese children's schools) cannot be hindered by the former. The current policy should still be temporarily followed, and schools should be established by the Council, taking into account the financial resources. At the same time, private schools, both Chinese and foreign, should be given subsidies according to the current method.

It is found that the original suggestions of the Japanese community include four items: (1) Stop running Council-run schools; (2) Provide subsidies to the schools of various foreign communities; (3) The annual amount of subsidies should be based on the educational budget for 1934 (including both regular and temporary items); (4) The distribution standard should be determined according to the number of students or the number of taxpayers.

During the consideration of the Education Committee, the Chinese members also submitted a written opinion, arguing that the original plan in 1931 should still be followed, and the benefits of increasing the number of schools should not be sacrificed by increasing subsidies. Subsidies can indeed reach a larger number of students, but increasing the number of Council-run schools is enough to improve the level of education. Therefore, both should not be neglected. The report submitted by the Director of Education in June also pointed out that the level of subsidized schools is generally lower, and the Council has not been able to directly intervene. Therefore, the advantages of subsidies still depend on the amount of fees and whether the supervisors of each school can cooperate closely. The opinion paper argued that the current policy should still be followed, and the eight-year construction plan should continue to be implemented. After the completion of this plan, it can accommodate 7.5% of Chinese students, but it is only enough to meet the minimum needs.

At a recent meeting of the Education Committee, the financial relationship between the opinion paper and the Japanese community's suggestions was discussed together. With regard to the original suggestion to use the construction fee drawn from public bonds in the temporary budget to allocate subsidies for routine expenses, it was considered inconsistent with financial principles and could damage the credibility of the Council.

In the Japanese community's letter of suggestion, it was pointed out that Council-run schools cost a lot, but only a small number of children benefit. In the opinion of the Chairman of the Committee, this should be remedied. The Director of Education recently had a plan to establish simpler schools, which is an effort in this regard. As for the issues of subsidies in the original letter of suggestion, they may not yet be well understood. In the opinion of the Director, the Council's policy already contains both the establishment of schools and subsidies. Although it has been implemented for three years, it is still in the experimental stage. As far as we can see at present, there seems to be no reason to sacrifice the school construction plan and greatly increase subsidies. On this point, the Director believes that the Chinese Committee's opinion paper is quite appropriate. However, one of the members of the Committee believes that the Council's eight-year construction plan has been finalized and cannot be changed. The original plan is temporary in nature and allows for reconsideration in the future.

After a detailed discussion among the members, it was considered that the Japanese community's suggestion could not be implemented, and the Board of Directors was asked to reply. The Board of Directors then resolved as above.

Construction of the Central Business District Is Rapidly Advancing; Groundbreaking Ceremony for the Municipal Library and Museum Is Held Simultaneously 204

Today at 2:00 PM

To Be Completed by the End of August Next Year

Culture and life cannot be separated for a moment. Cities are places where the population is concentrated, and cultural construction is especially urgent. The residents of Shanghai have reached more than 3.4 million, and the previous cultural facilities were either too small or simply non-existent, which is a pity. Wu Tiecheng, the Mayor of Shanghai, was aware of this, so he designated a vast area in the central business district as an administrative area, with a part of it for cultural facilities, and encouraged private groups to rent land here to establish exhibition venues related to culture and education. In January of this year, he also ordered the municipal government and most of its bureaus and departments to move into the central business district to work, leading by example and laying the groundwork for the realization of the Greater Shanghai Plan. Furthermore, as cultural construction cannot be delayed, in addition to preparing to build a municipal sports field in the southwest of the administrative area to meet the needs of citizens to exercise, the municipal library and museum will also be built in the administrative area as a source of learning and research for citizens. The municipal sports field, gymnasium, and swimming pool have already been laid and are under construction, and they are scheduled to be completed by the end of August next year. The groundbreaking ceremony for the two libraries and museums will also be held at 2:00 PM today. The construction and arrangement of one of the classes will be briefly described as follows:

Library 205

External Engineering: This library is located in the central business district administrative area, between Fuxing Stone Road and Funan Stone Road, south of Fuxiwai Road, facing west and east, opposite the museum. The plane is in the shape of a "work" character, and the two ends of the front part extend horizontally and protrude forward and backward, forming a wing room. The maximum distance between the north and south ends is about 66 meters, and the maximum distance between the east and west ends is about 51 meters. The construction area is about 1,620 square meters. The total area of each floor is about 3,470 square meters, and the volume is about 25,000 cubic meters. Most of this library is a two-story building, and the average height of the outer wall is about 12 meters. However, a gate tower is set up in the center of the front, and its ridge is about 25 meters above the ground. In the future, if there is a need for expansion, there is no need to raise the existing library building. It is only necessary to add houses of the same number of floors on the remaining land behind it to increase the capacity to more than twice.

Internal Engineering 206

Regarding the layout of the internal ground floor, the entrance in the center is a hall, about 12 meters wide and 13 meters deep, passing through the passages on both wings and the grand staircase to the upper floor. Behind the hall is the magazine and newspaper reading room, about 17 feet wide and 14 feet deep. Further back is the book storage room, about 30 meters wide and 11 meters deep, leading directly to the back door. This book storage room is a specially high one-story type (the outer wall is about 13.5 meters high), so as to install a five-story steel bookshelf of more than 2 meters high. The total length of the books arranged is about 15,000 meters, and it can hold about 400,000 volumes. The lower floor of the left wing is for various offices, and the lower floor of the right wing is for the children's library, the rare book storage room, and the lecture hall (about 10 meters wide and 18 meters long). The center of the second floor is divided into two parts. The front is the exhibition room, about 22 meters wide and 13.5 meters long. The back is the borrowing room and the catalog room, about 17 meters wide and the same length as the above. The left and right wings are the passage research room and the special reading room. The horizontal parts at both ends are reading rooms, about 26 meters wide and 10 meters long, each of which can accommodate 150 seats. Above the front of the center of the second floor, there is a mezzanine for storage. From here, you can reach the flat roof behind, and use the open-air steps to climb the gate tower. This gate tower can be used as an exhibition hall, and its surrounding platform can be used for climbing and overlooking the distance. A part of the magazine and newspaper reading room is excavated to build a basement for installing boilers.

Material Arrangement 207

Exterior of the Hall (see illustration): A hybrid style combining modern and Chinese architecture is adopted. Purely Chinese style would be too expensive and not entirely practical. The gatehouse is covered with yellow glazed tiles, adorned with magnificent ornaments. The surrounding platform garden features stone railings, fully displaying the characteristics of Chinese architecture. The entire building is constructed with steel reinforced concrete for fireproofing. The exterior walls are built with artificial stone. A large platform is set in front of the main entrance, planted with flowers and trees. Flagpoles are erected on either side of the platform to enhance the grandeur.

The interior of the main hall, reading room, and exhibition halls is decorated in a purely Chinese style of splendor. Vermilion columns are installed. The floors of the stairs and corridors are paved with polished stone. The floor of the reading room is covered with cork tiles, while the floors of other areas are covered with parquet flooring of oak and rubber tiles.

Expenditure Distribution 208

The project budget for this hall is 300,000 yuan, excluding the cost of steel bookshelves in the library. The construction project was awarded to Zhang Yutai, which began in September of the 23rd year [of the Republic] and is scheduled to be completed in August of the 24th year [of the Republic].

Museum 209

External Works: This hall is located in the city center administrative district, between Fuqian Left Road and Funan Left Road, facing west from the south side of Fudong Outer Road, opposite the library. The floor plan is similar to the library, but the two ends of the front wing only protrude slightly forward (see museum illustration). The maximum distance from north to south is approximately 68 feet, and the maximum distance from east to west is approximately 58 meters. The building area is approximately 1,900 square meters. The total area of each floor is approximately 3,430 square meters, with a volume of approximately 19,000 cubic meters. The central part and the front two wings of the main building are two-story structures with an exterior wall height of 10.5 meters. There is also a gatehouse, with a ridge height of approximately 24 meters. The protruding parts of the front two wings and the rear two wings are single-story structures, with an exterior wall height of approximately 6.5 meters (see front and side view illustrations of the museum). The future expansion plan of this hall also aims to add buildings on the remaining land, which can triple the building area after expansion.

Internal Works 210

Internally, the central entrance on the ground floor is the lobby, approximately 17.5 meters wide and 14 meters long. Attached are stairs to the upper floors and rooms for cloakroom and sales. Inward from here is the main hall, approximately 11.5 meters wide and 18 meters long, where the main staircase is located. On both sides of the main hall are corridors leading to the offices, research rooms, and storage rooms in the left and right wings of the front part. The protruding part of the left wing is the library, approximately 10 meters wide and 15 meters long, accommodating approximately 100 seats. The protruding part of the right wing is the lecture hall, with the same length and width as the library, accommodating approximately 300 seats. The layout of the second floor is divided into three parts as exhibition halls, the largest of which is the front left one, measuring approximately 17 meters wide and 14 meters long. The two wings are calligraphy and painting exhibition halls, each approximately 11.5 meters wide and 25 meters long, covered with glass skylights. Above the front exhibition hall on the central second floor is a mezzanine floor, level with the flat roof at the rear. From here, large open stairs lead to the gatehouse on the fourth floor. The gatehouse also has a platform around it for distant views. There is a basement under the lobby for the installation of boilers and other equipment.

Material arrangement: The appearance of the hall is roughly the same as the library, but the beams and columns of the gatehouse are exposed. Fountains are installed in front of the protruding parts of the left and right wings to enhance the appearance. The entire building is also a steel reinforced concrete fireproof structure, and the exterior walls are built with artificial stone. The interior decoration aims to create a suitable background for the exhibits. The lobby and main exhibition halls are decorated with red pillars and palace-style painted railings. Most of the floor is polished stone, while the floor of the important exhibition halls is inlaid with flower-patterned sandalwood. The corridors are also paved with polished stone. The lighting of each exhibition hall aims to project the most light onto the exhibits without reflecting into the eyes of the visitors. The area for hanging paintings is illuminated from above and the sides, allowing the light to shine obliquely on the wall, so that visitors can face the bright paintings in the shadows, making them brighter and clearer. The lighting equipment adopts the "indirect" style, with the same purpose as above. Since the upper exhibition halls do not have windows, but rely on glass skylights for lighting, artificial methods must be used to exchange air. The hall is equipped with ventilation equipment to distribute cold and warm air separately according to the changing seasons.

Expenditure Distribution: The project budget for this hall is 300,000 yuan. The construction project was also contracted by Zhang Yutai, which began in September of the 23rd year [of the Republic] and is scheduled to be completed in August of the 24th year [of the Republic].

The above description only concerns the engineering aspects of the library and museum in the city center area. As for the collection of books and magazines in the library and the acquisition of display specimens in the museum, efforts should be made to achieve perfection in order to meet the needs of promoting culture and to fulfill the purpose of building a great Shanghai. However, this matter is significant and cannot be accomplished overnight. It is said that Mayor Wu Tiecheng spares no effort in planning and managing the construction and prosperity of the entire city center area and the cultural needs of all Shanghai citizens. It is hoped that people from all walks of life will rise up to assist and witness its success together.

Free Talk

Literature and Life 218

— Lin Huanping

A few days ago, I received a letter from a poet who once exclaimed why he didn't follow the late poet Zhu Xiang. Inside, it said, "I always want to leave this so-called literary scene and become a shop assistant or a small clerk or something. First, it can solve the problem of livelihood; second, perhaps I can write different articles because of the changes in actual life. Otherwise, I will be desperate," etc. Reading it couldn't help but make me think of the difficulties of a literati's life, but mainly, it made me think of the importance of actual life in literature. I want to talk about this issue very simply here.

Indeed, observing life is not the same as experiencing it. There are indeed such people among our country's writers. Because they have no practical experience of life, they rely solely on the writer's subjective method of understanding to observe or even speculate. As a result, the life reflected in artistic works often has gaps or inconsistencies with actual life. Many examples of this can be found in the works produced in recent years. (Of course, there are also subjective conditions such as the artist's technique, but the lack of practical life experience can be said to be the main reason.) Therefore, now that I have read this poet's letter, as someone who is a poet and wants to become a shop assistant or a small clerk, I very much agree. An artist who can delve into the actual life of the people is always better than someone who hangs around in the so-called literary scene doing nothing. (The possibility and importance of observing life cannot be covered in this short article.)

In fact, artists cannot do without knowing life. They can only draw their own images from reality, from life. The richer their life experience, the richer their storage of images. Therefore, they will be able to create the necessary stories more freely for their own images and their own purposes. Gorky once said that the more complex and diverse an artist's life experience, the more he will be elevated and his horizons broadened. This is an unchangeable truth. Artists must depict the truth. They must embody reality in all its truth, in its contradictions, its direction of development, and in a historical perspective, in their artistic images. Artists must express the truth of life, its essence, through images of typical significance. They do not deal with general abstract laws that summarize various phenomena, but they deal with phenomena taken from individual objects or phenomena, and in the end, from direct life, and then grasp and describe the most typical phenomena in the form of sensory images. Only truthfulness is the prerequisite for all great works of art. Without complex and rich practical life experience, sensitive artistic sensibility, and correct methods, it is impossible to grasp the truth of reality in the way described above. The reason why Balzac is a greater artist than all the Zolas of the past, present, and future is precisely because in "The Human Comedy" he reflected the entirety of his era as clearly as if it were reflected in a mirror. And Balzac's ability to achieve this, needless to say, was also due to his rich life experience and his thorough method of analyzing reality, transforming objective social reality into concrete images contrary to his worldview. Sinclair's "The Jungle" is said to have been written after he spent some time working in a slaughterhouse. Most of Gorky's works, especially "Forty Years" and several autobiographical works such as "My Childhood," are records of his lived experiences.

Deeply immersing oneself in the torrent of social reality, closely observing, experiencing, and understanding life, and closely studying reality is a prerequisite for a great artist.

I look forward to the creation of great poems by the poet who wrote to me in the future.

"Spiritual Transformation" 219

— Hu Luo

Mr. Xiang Yu "believes that in the society of vulgar people, spiritual transformation is a child becoming a lion, and a lion becoming a camel." I still don't understand what he is afraid of about "camel." I have a good impression of "camel." I often think of a picture: a vast desert, camels carrying heavy objects, with perseverance, advancing step by step. Isn't this a symbol of life? Camels carrying the great mission of life, bravely moving forward. In the desert, there are certainly violent winds and a lack of water, but the camels ignore these, they must complete their mission. This is also a life of struggle, because camels have to fight against hunger, thirst, and violent winds. Therefore, the spiritual transformation of "child → lion → camel" is the most correct and meaningful process of life.

However, in this society of vulgar people, "spiritual transformation" is not as simple as Mr. Xiang Yu says. "Child → lion → camel" is precisely one type of spiritual transformation in a society of vulgar people. At the very least, we can find other spiritual transformations. In fact, this society is complex enough, and people's lives are also extremely complex. But society is not static after all, it is changing forward. In the process of change, we can discover many kinds of spiritual transformations. I think, in addition to the "child → lion → camel" spiritual transformation that chases after society, at least two other spiritual transformations can be discovered: "child → → → pig" and "child → lion → → etc." Naturally, there are other spiritual transformations, but these few are the most common and typical.

Lu Weifu, the protagonist in "In the Tavern," is a typical example of spiritual transformation. In his childhood, Lu Weifu "went to the City God Temple to pull off the beards of the statues," and also "argued about methods to reform China to the point of fighting." This was precisely the golden age of transforming from "child" to "lion." But as Lu Weifu gradually stepped into society, in the changing tides of society, after being washed over several times, he could only lose heart and decline. He said, "I am naturally much more numb now," "But I am like this now, just going through the motions, muddling along..." This is transforming from "lion" back into "pig." Aren't there many such people in today's society? They have lost the courage of their youth and are living a "pig"-like numb life, just waiting for the final slaughter. Aren't there many people in society who are shaking their heads and sighing, "Life is meaningless"? In fact, it is precisely because they have given up on life. Look, they are waving the banner of "living one day at a time." I ask, what is the difference between this and the life of a "pig"? Therefore, this kind of spiritual transformation is: "child → lion → pig."

Windy Night 220

— Zi Gang

Even the daytime is like nighttime, gloomy and hazy, with not a single ray of sunlight visible. At times like these, one feels that even the faintest, yellowish sunlight is as hot as an electric stove.

At night, the wind comes.

It roars wildly, making one think of those fur-clad friends in the deep mountains and forests, opening their huge, cave-like mouths and slowly stretching their bodies to howl at the sky. The long howl hides an invincible majesty.

One's nerves are like a worn-out leather bag, contracting and twitching, with cold air seeping into the pores: the shivering winter!

I'm sick, so weak.

Tightly wrapped in that cotton quilt that was thrown under the bed in the summer, the icy air drills in mercilessly. It would be best to be swaddled in a small quilt like a newborn baby, or like a corpse being tightly bound when put in a coffin. Hugging the flattened pillow, I smile enviously.

The ten-watt light bulb, which is usually considered too dim, seems too bright when I'm sick. Lying facing the light, the glare stings my eyes until they feel like they're about to burst with pain. Turning away, the white wall is just as stimulating to my vision. Let me close my eyes...

Like a kaleidoscope of flashing lights, everything sways around me, before and behind. I've turned into the thousand-eyed bodhisattva from mythology, light on the left, light on the right, light everywhere...

The wind has taken over the world!

Quietly, the leaves rustle, and one can hear the old tree trunks swaying. The leaves fall, chasing after each other, kissing the ground. Then the branches brace themselves again, with great strength!

I can guess that tomorrow morning, those two elm trees and the locust tree will definitely be as bald as a monk's head. This is the straightforwardness of the north. Yellow leaves can stay on the branches for a month or so, but a sudden gust of wind can blow them all away.

I forgot, there's also a raspberry bush in front of the window.

Even the door and windows become restless, unable to stand still, swaying back and forth: bang, bang... countless times. That window, which couldn't be closed a few days ago because the wood had swollen, was planed down a layer after borrowing a plane from the landlord's carpenter. Now that the wind has picked up, it's shrunk again and become loose.

Let them bang, anyway, the door is locked from the inside, so I'm not afraid of ghosts coming alone. I prop myself up and get out of bed, walk to the door and turn off the light. Although the light in the hallway is still shining in, it's faint after all. Oh, moonless windy night! I crawl back into the quilt, shivering continuously. The burning heat from the original illness has dissipated a bit, and a layer of cold air floats on my forehead. I press down on my chest, and a wave of nausea comes again. Small worms seem to be biting in my intestines, with a stinging pain.

Habitually, the landlord's radio is always playing at night. What was it singing? An old, long-forgotten "Falling Flowers and Flowing Water" plays again, I can't tell whose delicate voice it is.

Silently cursing the landlord's heartlessness, making noise all night long. And then...

"A person far away from home!" I mutter, pressing my face hard into the pillow. Isn't that so? The family letter that just arrived is still lying beside the pillow. On it is my father's half-open-eyed sigh, the decline and chaos of the end of the century: my younger brother's words, filled with sorrow, coming from his innocent heart. He understands people's struggles and hard work; hardship has made a child precocious and intelligent! In my mother's crooked handwriting, her deep love and pity are revealed, which covers up the suffering she has endured in the world.

Ivy-like thoughts entangle this sick heart.

While the wind dominates the world. Dim, rampant.

In my sleep, I gallop on the wings of the wind.

Tomorrow (5) 221

— Translated by Wu Xiangyu (Josepb Conrad)

Everything was delayed like that, and everything was being prepared for tomorrow in the same way. So many packets of flower seeds, enough to fill a box, had been selected and were ready to be planted in the front garden. "My dear, he will undoubtedly want you to participate in giving some advice on planting flowers," Captain Hagberd said to her, hinting, as he walked past the iron gate.

Miss Bessant lowered her head and concentrated on her work. She had heard all this many times. But often she would get up, put down her sewing, and slowly walk to the wooden fence. These gentle fibs also had some magic. He had decided that his son would never leave again because he had no home, and he had prepared a home for him. He had filled another small house with all sorts of furniture. She imagined it all brand new and painted, piled up like in a furniture store. There were several tables covered with coarse linen; several rolls of carpets, thick and upright, like parts of pillars, and white marble tips, revealing some light from the dark recesses. Captain Hagberd often described the items he had bought to her, just as he would to someone with a legitimate right to use them. Perhaps the barren patio of his small house could be paved with terrazzo... after tomorrow.

"We can even tear down the woodshed. You can hang your clothesline outside, and your flowers won't be spoiled." His eyes squinted, making her feel slightly ashamed.

The delusion that had infiltrated her life due to the compassionate impulse in her heart was not without reasonable circumstances. What would happen if his son came back one day? But she was not even sure if he had a son; even assuming he was somewhere, he was always far away. When Captain Hagberd aroused his emotions in his conversation, she had to pretend to believe him to calm him down, and even cover up her disapproval with a little smile.

Only once had she pointed out the doubtful nature of a hope that would ultimately lead to disappointment, but the end result of her attempt startled her greatly. The old man's face immediately showed extreme horror and distrust, as if he had seen a crack in the heavens.

"You... you... you don't believe he drowned, do you!"

For a moment, he, it seemed to her, was about to go mad again, because under normal circumstances, he was much more rational than people imagined. However, shortly after the emotional outburst, he would return to his previous extremely affectionate and gentle state.

"Don't be frightened, my dear," he said with a slight cunning, "the sea cannot hold him, he is not a seafaring man. None of us Hagberds are seafaring, just like me: I didn't drown. Besides, he's not a sailor at all; if he's not a sailor, he's bound to come back. There's nothing that can stop him from coming back."

His eyes started to squint again.

"Tomorrow."

She never said that again, for fear that the old man would go mad immediately. He depended on her. She seemed to be the only sensible person in town; he openly rejoiced in front of her that he was able to get such a calm wife for his son. The rest of the townspeople, he once said to her trustingly with some anger, are very strange in the way they look at you, the way they talk to you - he never got along with anyone in this place. Don't like these people. If his son hadn't liked Ercolbrook, he wouldn't have left his hometown.

Midnight Snack 222

— TK

The Gentry 223

— Shen Shengshi

I am a person who does not understand worldly affairs, nor do I know how to fawn over the local gentry. My social skills are at best those of a primary school student. When I meet those local gentry, my heart panics. And I am naturally not good at speaking. I really envy those friends who can talk, but although I am not good at chatting (meaningless chatting makes me dislike it from the bottom of my heart), my eyes do understand other people's hearts, and I often quietly describe a person in silence.

Normally, I don't associate much with the gentry, and I rarely visit them. Sometimes, when I encounter gentry on the street who have some connection with me, or who are relatives or my childhood teachers, I always greet them respectfully first. I don't care what expression they will reply with or whether they should even acknowledge me.

Indeed, gentry always have a gentry-like demeanor. They have special eyes to look at people. I sometimes foolishly think that I have already been seen by them as such and such. Let me guess! But there's no room for guessing. Many "facts" have proven to them that I am an improper youth, such as when I ran away from the store a few years ago; when I made trouble with the professors; and most recently, when I became unemployed (of course, in the eyes of the gentry, it's because I couldn't do anything well, and unemployment is only natural, and perhaps they all expect me to be begging on the streets in the near future). Also, I write poetry even though I am getting poorer. In a word, I clearly heard a certain gentleman snorting and cursing me:

"That kid deserves it!"

I don't want to defend myself about the so-called "deserving it" situation. They are gentry, and I dare not offend them!

I still have a breath of ambition, and a person who still has a little hope for himself will not die and should work hard. In poverty and ridicule, I must get up, like a small grass by the roadside, being stepped on by passersby, but it insists on nodding towards the sun.

Recently, at a certain occasion, I had the opportunity to meet with those gentry again. They all looked at me with contempt, which was only natural! In the gentry's gatherings, I am always coldly treated by them.

Several "young masters" of the gentry were my childhood classmates, and now they are of course university students under the foreign dignitaries. They also have an air of gentry, which I don't admire much. They are not yet worthy of being gentry. In the future, I can't guarantee that they will definitely become gentry. The old gentry will die, the era will move forward, and the gentry's gold medal may lose its luster.

Correction: In the second section, first line, of Mr. Zang Kejia's poem "Elegy" published in this journal on November 22, the word "歲" (sui, year) in "剝開守歲的心的年輪中" (peeling open the annual rings of the heart guarding the year), was originally written in simplified form as "止不." The typesetter carved this character as is and put it in. The proofreader did not correct it, and the editor was also lazy and did not correct it in the next day's issue. Who knew it would be misunderstood, so we must quickly clarify it to avoid further misunderstandings.
