Special Issue on the International Grand Hotel

The Origin of the International Grand Hotel 224

While there are many Chinese-owned hotels in Shanghai, there is a distinct lack of facilities for accommodating foreign guests. Nowadays, with the intermingling of cultures and the increasing number of foreign tourists visiting China, our country lacks suitable accommodations to entertain guests from afar. Consequently, the lodging, dining, and all other hospitality matters are still entrusted to Western-owned hotels, which is quite regrettable. Therefore, the new high-rise building of the Joint Savings Society, the only one of its kind in the Far East, was leased to organize the International Grand Hotel Co., Ltd. to operate a new hotel business and remedy this deficiency. The address is centrally located, the architecture is magnificent, the layout is novel, and the service is meticulous. It is in no way inferior to any foreign-owned residence in Shanghai. The characteristics are briefly listed below:

(1) Architectural Excellence: The building stands majestically at the corner of Bubbling Well Road and Nanking Road, facing south towards the Racecourse, occupying more than two acres of land. Towering into the clouds, it offers a panoramic view of Shanghai. The scenery of Wusong and Longhua, with their clouds and trees, seems to be right before one's eyes. Even distant Kunshan and Sheshan are faintly visible. The entire twenty-two-story building is constructed entirely of steel and concrete, standing three hundred feet above the ground. It was designed by the local architect Hudec, and the latest architectural principles were adopted for the light and air throughout the building. The exterior is clad in domestically produced black granite, and the interior is also lined with precious jade-green marble. A 700-foot-deep artesian well has been drilled to supply water to the entire building. It can truly be called the culmination of modern architectural excellence.

(2) Room Amenities: The hotel has a total of over two hundred rooms, divided into single and double rooms. Single rooms all have a cloakroom and washroom, while double rooms also have a sitting room. All decorations incorporate the best of Chinese and Western styles. Rental fees are calculated on a daily or monthly basis, according to the convenience of the customer. It has the characteristics of a Western-owned hotel, but with lower prices and greater comfort.

(3) Installation of New-Style Elevators: These new-style elevators are also the first of their kind to be installed in Shanghai. They can travel six hundred feet per minute, so it takes only half a minute to go from the bottom floor to the roof. Each floor is marked with illuminated indicators that are clearly visible. The same markings are also installed inside the elevator so that passengers can see which floor they have reached. The opening and closing of the elevator doors are automatic. There are a total of three elevators for customer use, and two more for transporting luggage and servants.

(4) Allocation of the Entire Building: The ground floor houses the Joint Savings Society's all-steel vault and various mechanical rooms. The first floor is the headquarters of the Society and its various departments. The second floor is the grand dining hall. The third floor is the kitchen and arcade. The fourth to thirteenth floors are the hotel's various rooms. The fourteenth floor is the small dining hall and rooftop garden. The fifteenth to eighteenth floors are beautifully decorated and well-furnished apartments. The nineteenth floor is the directors' office. The twentieth and twenty-first floors have water tanks in the center. The roof is used by the Municipal Council to establish a fire lookout tower for the protection of the people of Shanghai.

(5) Organizational Outline: The following gentlemen serve as directors of the International Grand Hotel Co., Ltd.:

Mr. Yan Huiqing

Mr. Wang Zhengting

Mr. Chen Guangfu

Mr. Gui Yanfang

Mr. Wu Daquan

Mr. Zhou Zuomin

Mr. Hu Bijiang

Mr. Xu Hanqing

Mr. Qian Xinzhi

Mr. Shi Boqun

Mr. Xiang Zhongyong

Mr. Wang Ertao

Mr. Lu Shoulian

From among the directors, five executive directors are elected to preside over all personnel and administrative matters:

Mr. Qian Xinzhi

Mr. Shi Boqun

Mr. Xiang Zhongyong

Mr. Wang Ertao

Mr. Gui Yanfang

Supervisors:

Mr. Chen Jie

Mr. Zhou Di

Mr. Min Dihua

(6) Organizational Features

A. Training of Attendants: The hotel has established a training center to promote vocational education and in view of the lack of training for attendants in various hotels in China. One hundred and eighty young people who have graduated from schools are selected and taught hotel application knowledge, focusing on courtesy, demeanor, and physical education. They are also trained to be patient, quick, and hygienic. The teachers hired are all specialized experts. Each student undergoes more than six months of academic training and practical experience, and is assigned to serve in the hotel. Those with excellent performance are promoted to higher levels. This opens up new career paths for young people. Dormitories are built on Zhongshan Road and a large sports field is built to ensure the physical and mental health of the attendants in order to train these specialized talents. The scale of this endeavor is probably unimaginable.

B. Exquisite Cuisine: Special types of utensils and equipment are ordered from British and American factories. The equipment is exquisite and unique, much of which has never been seen in Shanghai before, such as various pure silver tableware from the Austrian Berndorf factory and automatic dishwashers from famous American factories. A famous French chef is specially hired to preside over the dining affairs, which will surely refresh our palates in the future.

C. Comprehensive Facilities: The hotel has spent a huge sum of money and two years of time to adopt the latest Chinese and Western inventions and the most luxurious equipment, such as air conditioning, carpets, etc. The furniture is manufactured by the famous Shanghai companies of Mayar, Taison, and Sincere, using high-grade wood such as Austrian beech and teak, sprayed with transparent and colorless paint. Each strives to create unique designs. The stair railings are decorated with carved steel, and the walkways are covered with five-color rubber carpets. In short, the purchase of every item and the installation of every device has been carefully considered and reformed by experts several times to ensure comfort, quietness, cleanliness, and beauty.

D. Public Spaces: (1) The Grand Dining Hall is spacious and grand, with textured beech wood paneling and various recessed lights and artistic paint, creating a magnificent effect. (2) The Small Dining Hall is paneled with Austrian beech wood and inlaid with silver silk brocade curtains, with colors that harmonize with the walls and furniture, in accordance with artistic principles. (3) The arcade has a black marble corridor platform paired with white metal railings, with a clear distinction between black and white. The teak wood paneling is inlaid with chemically refined steel, and the sunset reflects the gold-colored carved copper pillars, creating fantastic colors. (4) The rooftop garden connects to the stars above and overlooks the bustling city below, gathering flowers and plants, which is truly a human paradise. Other features such as the tea room also have their own characteristics. It is naturally the best place for large banquets, and also a scenic spot for small gatherings and conversations.

(7) Management Personnel: Mr. Schubla, the former manager of the Astor House Hotel, has been specially hired as the manager. He has extensive experience and is capable of making proper arrangements. Those who know him are all pleased to have such a capable person. The staff in each department are also specialized talents with rich experience. The opening date is not far off, and it will soon be filled with carriages and horses, crowded on Bubbling Well Road.

The tallest 22-story building in the Eastern Hemisphere was constructed by Fook Kee Construction Company

A Visit to Fook Kee Construction Company 225

— Reporter

The height of the 22-story building of the Joint Savings Society is a creation for the Eastern Hemisphere. Shanghai had never seen it before. All construction companies lacked experience, and the Joint Savings Society did not want to rely on foreigners. After several considerations, it did not use the bid price as a criterion, but relied on reputation and experience. Therefore, Fook Kee Construction Company was able to obtain the construction rights without the lowest bid price. Now the building has been completed, standing tall and majestically overlooking the sea. This is indeed the unique vision of the Joint Savings Society, but the spirit of struggle of Fook Kee is also commendable. The reporter does not hesitate to be verbose and now publishes the general situation of the company in the newspaper for the research of entrepreneurs. Fook Kee Construction Company was founded solely by Mr. Tao Guilin. Mr. Tao is from Nantong. He lost his father when he was young, and his family was poor and he could not study. At the age of twelve, he came to Shanghai to learn crafts. He was very hardworking and did not indulge in bad habits. He was also frugal and thrifty. With a little savings, he founded the company.

In the beginning, the scale was very small and the reputation was not well-known, so there were not many projects undertaken. Before the company was founded, Mr. Tao had worked in the construction industry for fifteen years, working hard and studying carefully. He realized that the poor organization of Chinese construction companies and the conservatism of construction technology allowed foreign construction companies to rise and thrive. Therefore, he had the idea of organizing his own company, but he was limited by financial resources and could not fulfill his ambition. After the company was established, the initial capital was only 50,000 yuan. Mr. Tao devoted himself to management, striving for scientific organization and artistic construction techniques, while also paying attention to solidity and durability. He also adhered to the principle of low profits, and sometimes even sacrificed profits. Therefore, the projects he built, such as the Jiande Savings Society, the China Wharf, and the Shilong Hospital, were all very satisfactory to the owners. In a few years, his reputation grew greatly. In 1928, he won the bid to build the Guangzhou Sun Yat-sen Memorial Hall, and his business flourished like a bamboo pole rising in the sun, and his name became well-known.

Because the original company address was not enough for office space, in 1929, the head office was established on Jiujiang Road. Later, with the increasing development of the business and the increasing number of employees, the original location was not enough, so in 1930, it was moved to the Enterprise Building on Sichuan Road.

Mr. Tao also realized that construction executives tended to be experienced but lacked academic knowledge. Therefore, he generously donated money to establish a vocational junior high school in his hometown of Lvsi, Nantong. It opened in the autumn of 1930, specializing in teaching civil engineering and architectural subjects, and opened a workshop for practical training. In order to cultivate poor children, the fees were extremely low, so the annual burden of regular expenses was quite large. In the summer of 1933, the first class graduated. Mr. Tao arranged positions for them one by one, and no one was left out.

Moreover, Mr. Tao had great ambitions, and his business was not limited to Shanghai. The Guangzhou Sun Yat-sen Memorial Hall, the Xiamen American Consulate, the Haizhou Barracks, the Henan Arsenal Branch, the Qingdao Shipyard, the Guixi Iron Bridge in Zhejiang, the Zhongzheng Bridge in Jiangxi, and the Lishi Society, the Chongqing Meifeng Bank, and the Huaiyin Diversion Sluice Project were all built by the company. His business was almost half of China, and the capital amount had been successively increased to 400,000 yuan. His organization and management were also very perfect. The head factory was located on Gordon Road in this city, the first factory was located on Guanglin Street in Zhabei, the second factory was located in Qingning Temple in Pudong, and the head office was located on Sichuan Road. There were no less than dozens of branches and branch offices, with hundreds of employees, including more than ten with a bachelor's degree in civil engineering, and countless people with rich experience. The factory was only established for ten years, and the construction projects had reached more than 15 million yuan. Now the process of undertaking the construction of the Joint Savings Society is described in detail below:

Installation of Steel Frame: The installation of the steel frame was the first step in the company's construction of this project. All the beams, columns, and internal materials were pure steel frames. The construction method used two machine cranes to alternately use to erect the steel frame. Each crane had a lifting capacity of seven and a half tons, and the rivets were compressed air. This project started on August 16, 1932. The first two layers of steel frames were erected, and after accurately measuring and verifying the entire level, they were successively connected upwards. On average, one layer was connected every three days, but after reaching the fourteenth floor, due to changes in the drawings and the fact that the manufacturers could not supply materials on schedule, it was delayed, and it was not completed until mid-April 1933.

Concrete Engineering: After the steel frame was erected, the concrete engineering began. Therefore, this project was the second step in the company's work. The concrete was mixed by machine. The ingredients were accurately mixed according to regulations, and dry mixing was performed several times before adding water to avoid excessive moisture. Therefore, the concrete floor made according to the instructions weighed 80 pounds per square foot, and the designer and the engineers of the Engineering Bureau proved through testing that it could bear more than 350 pounds per square foot, which also showed the company's serious attitude towards things.

All the bottoms of the steel frames and the surroundings of the connection with the foundation were filled with mortar. The rest was 124 concrete. The surrounding area was an average of two inches thick, but the middle of the I-shaped column head was filled with hollow bricks to reduce the weight of the concrete. The thickness of the floor varied depending on the distance between the beams, ranging from about four inches to five and a half inches. As a result, the floor with a 23-foot span was subjected to extremely heavy pressure, and there was no movement. This work rate was about one layer that could be completed in ten days, and it took about six months.

Partitions: Partitions were the third step in the project. In order to reduce weight, all internal partitions were made of aerated concrete bricks. When paving, the aerated concrete bricks were first moistened with water, and then cemented with 13 cement mortar. The top of the paving, and the joints with the concrete floor, or beams and columns, were filled with steel wedges to make the wall stable and not easy to shake. The wall surface was plastered with a layer of 13 cement mortar to protect the aerated bricks so that they would not expand and contract due to changes in climate. Outside the cement mortar, cane board was used to isolate sound waves. The board was then plastered with hemp ash and a layer of gypsum to make it smooth and beautiful.

Fourth Floor Reception Room 226

A Glimpse of the American-Style Bar in the Fourth Floor 227

The Fifteenth Floor Dining Room 228

Flat Roof: This project varies in its approach due to the different needs of each floor; the first, second, third and fourteenth floors have suspended steel wire mesh flat roofs, the style of which can be the first of its kind in Shanghai. The other flat roofs, concrete floors, are plastered with a layer of hemp ash and a layer of gypsum on the bottom. The flat roof on the thirteenth floor, due to ventilation and various pipes, is plastered with a layer of 13 ash sand on the suspended steel wire mesh, and then plastered with hemp ash and gypsum. This project, due to its large area and elaborate decoration, was quite difficult to construct: its patterns were complex and its appearance was beautiful, not only rare in Shanghai, but also pioneering in Asia.

Roof: The roof of the building is all flat concrete floors; about four and a half inches to five and a half inches thick. This concrete is mixed with water-repellent slurry when mixing. The upper layer of the roof is laid with eight layers of tar paper, and the felt is made of artificial stone roof. The flat roof on the thirteenth floor is nailed with a layer of cork two inches thick to prevent the sun from exposing and heating it.

Facing Brick: The facing bricks used in this project are all colored tank bricks; using 12 cement mortar mixed with water-repellent slurry, posted on the outer wall of steel bone concrete. The inside of the wall is painted with water-repellent paint, tank bricks to give over The surface is very difficult to work with because it needs to be flat; and the corners of sharp corners and small columns must be on a straight line.

Scaffolding: The scaffolding for this project is different from ordinary ones because it is more than 260 feet above the ground; all of its construction and installation uses 12-inch square wood, iron threads, etc., and is connected to the steel frame on all sides, and is wrapped with bamboo fences. Every three layers must have insurance bamboo fence equipment to prevent workers from falling. In summary, this project took two years and two months, and its difficulty and complexity are unspeakable: the house is high and finished, and the decoration is extremely elaborate and can be said to be a great project unprecedented in Shanghai. However, the factory was able to complete the project with caution, and it was able to have a safe guarantee for the workers, which is really commendable. It is heard that the building of the Da Xin Department Store Co., Ltd. in this city is also being constructed by the factory.

Talking about the Color of the Building Yuanfeng Company Paint Manufacturing Factory Paint Decoration Engineering Department 229

General Discussion: Why are there so many tall buildings in the city? It is said that transportation is convenient, personnel are busy, products are concentrated here, and capital technology is cooperatively available here. The strength of the country is crystallized here. The city is the general meeting of all industries, and the tall building is the center of various industries. The tall buildings are densely packed enough to brighten the city, and there is no need to build a tall building without the prosperity of all industries. Tall buildings are almost a microcosm of the country. Its style is sufficient to represent the character and spirit of the people, and its physique is sufficient to represent the manufacturing efficiency of the people. A brick, a tile, a stone, a wood, a nail, a pipe, and the degree of science and engineering knowledge of the people are measured here. The distribution of its usable ground, the office area, the dining hall area, the public area, the electromechanical water vapor ventilation fire protection and other equipment area, the hall area, and the recreational reading room area are all reflective of the customs of the contemporary people. The design and selection of materials must be extremely precise, and the coloring project is even more fundamental and important. Elegant distinction, identification should be clear, construction procedures, supervision should be strict, the safety and appearance of the entire department are tied to it,

Examine the important building materials, soil, wood, gold paint, the first three are essential materials before construction, the latter is the coloring agent after construction, it is also the clothing of the object, so as to prevent collapse, failure, corrosion and strengthen the appearance. Water vapor carbon nourishing, fiber formed by photochemistry, the elements of wood, from afforestation to logging, until the formation of beams, desks, doors, windows, floors, artificial several guarantees, once invaded by sunlight and moisture, corruption and annihilation, still cannot be distinguished by the eyes of water vapor carbon nourishing, the topic of destruction, cement combined with steel and iron, beautiful also,

Page 23

Beginning 230

The permeation of moisture, freezing when encountering cold, is followed by expansion and cracking. Humidity and air further reach the steel frame directly through the cracks, expanding due to rust, enlarging the cracks, and ultimately leading to collapse. This is also a regret in construction. Clothing and objects are precisely for avoiding the ravages of the natural world. A layer of paint film is no different from an insulator between steel, earth, and air. It is a protective film. This is the first way in which the coloring project is connected to the safety of the building. Paint is a product of modern science, with types varying according to their functions, with distinctions between protecting metal, wood, and earth. The construction procedure is extremely important. If the metal surface is not de-rusted and is directly coated with metal-protecting paint, it is no different from decorating rust with paint. Before long, the rust will fall off, and the paint will also fall off. If the concrete has not dried thoroughly and is directly coated with earth-protecting paint, or if it has dried thoroughly but has not undergone a sealing procedure, and is directly coated with earth-protecting paint, it is no different from destroying the paint with alkali. Or, if paint is applied to a wet surface, if the wood has not been thoroughly dried, or if the knots have not undergone a degreasing procedure, or if the wood holes have not been filled, and wood-protecting paint is directly applied, it is no different from applying paint to grease, or applying oil to a wet surface. Blistering, discoloration, grease penetration, brittleness, peeling, all kinds of paint film diseases are due to the disorder of the procedure. Conversely, it will be smooth and beautiful, pleasing to the eye, and earth, wood, and metal paint will each be in their proper place. This is the second way in which the coloring project is connected to the appearance of the building.

Examples

(A) Classification of Painted Surfaces

(1) First Category... Bedrooms, offices, libraries, assembly halls, etc.

(2) Second Category... Kitchens, bathrooms, elevator shafts, corridors, machine rooms, boiler rooms, etc.

(B) Material Selection

(1) First Category surfaces emphasize beauty.

For earthen surfaces, use matte paint. White is preferred for ceilings, and light colors are preferred for walls.

For wooden surfaces, use high-gloss enamel.

(2) Second Category surfaces, in addition to beauty, must also consider sturdiness and durability.

For earth, wood, and metal surfaces, use high-gloss paint.

(C) Material Specifications

(1) Matte Wall Paint

Solid... The main color material must not be less than 85 percent.

Liquid... Must contain an appropriate amount of boiled oil, suitable water thinner, and drying agent.

Coloring oil... Must contain pure raw materials.

(2) High-Gloss Paint

Solid... Full amount of the main color material.

Liquid... Same as (1)

Coloring oil... Same as (1)

(3) Enamel Primer

Solid... The main color material must not be less than 80 percent.

Liquid... Same as (1)

(4) Enamel

Solid... Full amount of the main color material.

Liquid... Varnish and thinner.

(5) Steel Primer

Solid... Full amount of rust-preventive color material.

Liquid... Pure oil and thinner.

(D) Painting Procedure

(1) Overview

1. Temperature... Must not be lower than 40 degrees Fahrenheit or higher than burning heat.

2. Ventilation... Adequate.

3. Surface... Thoroughly dry and clean.

4. Time... The first layer must not be painted with the second layer until it is dry. At least 48 hours.

Double Room 231

(2) Earthen Surface Painting Procedure

1. Surface preparation: Earthen surfaces should be dried for at least 30 days in the most suitable ventilation conditions. After cleaning, apply a sealant, then dry for another four days. Clean and prepare.

2. Film... Boiled oil and matte paint are used together. Uneven areas must be repainted until the whole is consistently smooth and even.

3. Topcoat... Two coats of matte paint, or one coat of high-gloss paint.

(3) Wooden Surface Painting Procedure

1. Surface Preparation... Resinous knots must be burned off and cleaned with turpentine one hour before painting.

2. Primer... Same as (2) with the addition of thinner.

3. Primer...

4. One or the following:

5. High-gloss paint... Apply two coats consecutively after applying the primer (2).

(4) Steel Painting Procedure

1. Surface Preparation... Rust must be removed with a chisel or wire brush, and oil must be washed away with gasoline.

2. Primer... Use steel primer.

3. Single gloss... Use two coats of high-gloss paint, or two coats of enamel primer, and one coat of enamel.

Record of the Completion of the Four Banks Vault 233

— Shujie

The Strongest and Largest Vault in the East

Designed and Built by Shanghai New Universal Company

Since the dynastic change, bandit disasters have been frequent. Prosperous families have invariably moved the treasures they formerly buried underground to steel boxes and cabinets to prevent the covetousness of petty thieves. Recently, with the Eastern spread of European trends, the skills of thieves have improved daily. The wise have gradually realized that iron boxes and locks are not enough to defend against the attacks of scientific methods. Those who have precious collections are all worried and mutually seek more reliable protection. Therefore, the establishment of a vault has arisen in response to the times. Originally, vault door equipment was designed for banks to protect their own funds. Later, as social mores deteriorated and thieves proliferated, individuals had limited financial resources and could not install large vaults at home. Therefore, they adhered to the principle of collective effort and rented them from others. Initially, only those related to banks enjoyed its benefits. However, due to the frequent needs of society, a special storage department was established to become a public storage institution.

The new vault of the Four Banks Savings Society was designed and built by the Shanghai New Universal Company, a purely Chinese-owned organization, after the association's architects Sun Liji and engineer Wu Qingquan, along with foreign architect Udal, thoroughly discussed various new and old robbery defense methods before the construction. The company is a vault and bank protection expert in Shanghai and has been engaged in this project for more than ten years. More than half of the financial assets in the Shanghai banking industry are under the company's strict planning and protection. This project was carefully planned by vault design expert, my classmate Yuan Pilie. Under the guidance of the famous architectural engineer, it felt even more like handling a familiar task with ease. It is the strongest and largest vault project in East Asia. Having been invited to visit, I dare to record its outline as follows.

The new vault of the Four Banks is located under the bottom floor of the new building. The purpose of a vault is to prevent theft and also to prevent disasters. Among cities, fire and war are the most common disasters. The new vault
